Its output are the broker\n44:  * state and various futures that can be used to wait for broker state transitions to\n45:  * occur.\n46:  *\n47:  * The lifecycle manager handles registering the broker with the controller, as described\n48:  * in KIP-631. \n108: /**\n109:  * Abstract Herder implementation which handles connector/task lifecycle tracking. Extensions\n110:  * must invoke the lifecycle hooks appropriately.\n111:  * <p>\n112:  * This class takes the following approach for sending status updates to the backing store:\n113:  *\n114:  * <ol>\n115:  * <li>\n116:  *    When the connector or task is starting, we overwrite the previous state blindly. This ensures that\n117:  *    every rebalance will reset the state of tasks to the proper state. The intuition is that there should\n118:  *    be less chance of write conflicts when the worker has just received its assignment and is starting tasks.\n119:  *    In particular, this prevents us from depending on the generation absolutely. If the group disappears\n120:  *    and the generation is reset, then we'll overwrite the status information with the older (and larger)\n121:  *    generation with the updated one. The danger of this approach is that slow starting tasks may cause the\n122:  *    status to be overwritten after a rebalance has completed.\n123:  *\n124:  * <li>\n125:  *    If the connector or task fails or is shutdown, we use {@link StatusBackingStore#putSafe(ConnectorStatus)},\n126:  *    which provides a little more protection if the worker is no longer in the group (in which case the\n127:  *    task may have already been started on another worker). Obviously this is still racy. If the task has just\n128:  *    started on another worker, we may not have the updated status cached yet. In this case, we'll overwrite\n129:  *    the value which will cause the state to be inconsistent (most likely until the next rebalance). Until\n130:  *    we have proper producer groups with fenced groups, there is not much else we can do.\n131:  * </ol>\n132:  */\n133: public abstract class AbstractHerder implements Herder, TaskStatus.Listener, ConnectorStatus.Listener {\n134: \n135:     private static final Logger log = LoggerFactory.getLogger(AbstractHerder.class);\n136: \n137:     private final String workerId;\n138:     protected final Worker worker;\n139:     private final String kafkaClusterId;\n140:     protected final StatusBackingStore statusBackingStore;\n141:     protected final ConfigBackingStore configBackingStore;\n142:     private volatile boolean ready = false;\n143:     private final Plugin<ConnectorClientConfigOverridePolicy> connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin;\n144:     private final ExecutorService connectorExecutor;\n145:     private final Time time;\n146:     protected final Loggers loggers;\n147: \n148:     private final CachedConnectors cachedConnectors;\n149: \n150:     public AbstractHerder(Worker worker,\n151:                           String workerId,\n152:                           String kafkaClusterId,\n153:                           StatusBackingStore statusBackingStore,\n154:                           ConfigBackingStore configBackingStore,\n155:                           ConnectorClientConfigOverridePolicy connectorClientConfigOverridePolicy,\n156:                           Time time) {\n157:         this.worker = worker;\n158:         this.worker.herder = this;\n159:         this.workerId = workerId;\n160:         this.kafkaClusterId = kafkaClusterId;\n161:         this.statusBackingStore = statusBackingStore;\n162:         this.configBackingStore = configBackingStore;\n163:         this.connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin = Plugin.wrapInstance(\n164:                 connectorClientConfigOverridePolicy,\n165:                 worker.metrics().metrics(),\n166:                 WorkerConfig.CONNECTOR_CLIENT_POLICY_CLASS_CONFIG);\n167:         this.connectorExecutor = Executors.newCachedThreadPool();\n168:         this.time = time;\n169:         this.loggers = Loggers.newInstance(time);\n170:         this.cachedConnectors = new CachedConnectors(worker.getPlugins());\n171:     }\n172: \n173:     @Override\n174:     public String kafkaClusterId() {\n175:         return kafkaClusterId;\n176:     }\n177: \n178:     protected abstract int generation();\n179: \n180:     protected void startServices() {\n181:         this.worker.start();\n182:         this.statusBackingStore.start();\n183:         this.configBackingStore.start();\n184:     }\n185: \n186:     protected void stopServices() {\n187:         this.statusBackingStore.stop();\n188:         this.configBackingStore.stop();\n189:         this.worker.stop();\n190:         this.connectorExecutor.shutdown();\n191:         Utils.closeQuietly(this.connectorClientConfigOverridePolicyPlugin, \"connector client config override policy\");\n192:     }\n193: \n194:     protected void ready() {\n195:         this.ready = true;\n196:     }\n197: \n198:     @Override\n199:     public boolean isReady() {\n200:         return ready;\n201:     }\n202: \n203:     @Override\n204:     public void onStartup(String connector) {\n205:         statusBackingStore.put(new ConnectorStatus(connector, ConnectorStatus.State.RUNNING,\n206:                 workerId, generation(), worker.connectorVersion(connector)));\n207:     }\n208: \n209:     @Override\n210:     public void onStop(String connector) {\n211:         statusBackingStore.put(new ConnectorStatus(connector, AbstractStatus.State.STOPPED,\n212:                 workerId, generation(), worker.connectorVersion(connector)));\n213:     }\n214: \n215:     @Override\n216:     public void onPause(String connector) {\n217:         statusBackingStore.put(new ConnectorStatus(connector, ConnectorStatus.State.PAUSED,\n218:                 workerId, generation(), worker.connectorVersion(connector)));\n219:     }\n220: \n221:     @Override\n222:     public void onResume(String connector) {\n223:         statusBackingStore.put(new Each instance of DistributedHerder joins the group and indicates what its current\\n135:  *     configuration state is (where it is in the configuration log). Most importantly, this includes writing updated configurations for connectors and tasks,\\n144:  *     (and therefore, also for creating, destroy, and scaling up/down connectors).\\n145:  * </p>\\n146:  * <p>\\n147:  *     The DistributedHerder uses a single thread for most of its processing. workers to spread work across multiple processes.\n131:  * </p>\n132:  * <p>\n133:  *     Under the hood, this is implemented as a group managed by Kafka's group membership facilities (i.e. the generalized\n134:  *     group/consumer coordinator). Each instance of DistributedHerder joins the group and indicates what its current\n135:  *     configuration state is (where it is in the configuration log). The group coordinator selects one member to take\n136:  *     this information and assign each instance a subset of the active connectors & tasks to execute. The assignment\n137:  *     strategy depends on the {@link ConnectAssignor} used. Once an assignment is received, the DistributedHerder simply\n138:  *     runs its assigned connectors and tasks in a {@link Worker}.\n139:  * </p>\n140:  * <p>\n141:  *     In addition to distributing work, the DistributedHerder uses the leader determined during the work assignment\n142:  *     to select a leader for this generation of the group who is responsible for other tasks that can only be performed\n143:  *     by a single node at a time. Most importantly, this includes writing updated configurations for connectors and tasks,\n144:  *     (and therefore, also for creating, destroy, and scaling up/down connectors).\n145:  * </p>\n146:  * <p>\n147:  *     The DistributedHerder uses a single thread for most of its processing. This includes processing\n148:  *     config changes, handling task rebalances and serving requests from the HTTP layer. The latter are pushed\n149:  *     into a queue until the thread has time to handle them. A consequence of this is that requests can get blocked\n150:  *     behind a worker rebalance. When the herder knows that a rebalance is expected, it typically returns an error\n151:  *     immediately to the request, but this is not always possible (in particular when another worker has requested\n152:  *     the rebalance). Similar to handling HTTP requests, config changes which are observed asynchronously by polling\n153:  *     the config log are batched for handling in the work thread.\n154:  * </p>\n155:  */\n156: Instead, services implement start() and stop() methods following a consistent pattern.\\n\\n### Key Lifecycle Components\\n\\n#### 1. Kafka Connect Runtime (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/)\\n**Connect.java** (lines 65-97): The main orchestrator that manages the complete lifecycle of a Kafka Connect process.\\n- **start()**: Initializes components in order\\n  - Registers shutdown hook\\n  - Calls herder.start()\\n  - Calls rest.initializeResources()\\n- **stop()**: Stops components in reverse order (rest → herder)\\n- **ShutdownHook** (inner class): Thread that ensures graceful shutdown\\n\\n**Herder.java** (lines 64-66): Interface defining the lifecycle contract\\n- void start()\\n- void stop()\\n\\n**AbstractHerder.java** (lines 180-192): Abstract implementation providing templated lifecycle\\n- startServices(): Coordinates startup of worker, statusBackingStore, configBackingStore\\n- stopServices(): Coordinates shutdown in reverse order with proper error handling\\n\\n**Worker.java** (lines 235-285): Manages individual worker lifecycle\\n- start(): Initializes globalOffsetBackingStore, metrics, and offset committer\\n- stop(): Gracefully stops all connectors and tasks, then cleans up resources with timeout handling\\n\\n**RestServer.java** (lines 200-394): Abstract REST server implementation\\n- initializeServer(): Starts Jetty server, configures handlers and contexts\\n- stop(): Gracefully stops all handlers, REST extensions, and Jetty server with resource cleanup\\n\\n**DistributedHerder.java** (lines 156-300): Implements distributed coordination\\n- Uses AtomicBoolean stopping flag for thread-safe shutdown\\n- Manages WorkerGroupMember coordination\\n- Handles executor service shutdown with timeouts\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Concrete implementation of RestServer\\n\\n#### 2. Stop transaction coordinator\\n  5. Stop group/share coordinators\\n  6. Stop replica manager\\n  7. Shutdown alter partition manager\\n  8. Close log manager and remote storage\\n  9. Stop quota managers\\n  10. Final socket server shutdown\\n  11. Close lifecycle manager\\n\\n**BrokerLifecycleManager.scala** (lines 223-307): Manages broker state machine lifecycle\\n- **start()**: Sends StartupEvent through event queue\\n  - Initializes channel manager\\n  - Transitions to STARTING state\\n  - Sends broker registration\\n- **beginControlledShutdown()**: Graceful shutdown request\\n- **beginShutdown()**: Non-blocking shutdown initiation\\n- **close()**: Blocks until complete shutdown\\n- Event-driven architecture using KafkaEventQueue for thread-safe operations\\n\\n**KafkaRaftServer.scala**: Combined controller/broker with startup() and shutdown() methods\\n- Implements reverse-order shutdown: broker first, then controller\\n\\n#### 3. Startup Ordering\\nServices are started in dependency order:\\n- Herder (manages everything)\\n  - Worker (manages connectors/tasks)\\n    - GlobalOffsetBackingStore\\n    - StatusBackingStore\\n    - ConfigBackingStore\\n  - REST server (depends on herder being ready)\\n\\n#### 2. Shutdown Ordering (Reverse Dependency Order)\\nServices are stopped in reverse order to their startup:\\n- REST server (stops accepting requests first)\\n- Herder (stops managing work)\\n  - Worker (stops connectors/tasks)\\n  - Backing stores\\n  - Status/Config stores\\n\\n#### 3. Error Handling Patterns\\n- **Try-finally blocks**: Ensure shutdown code runs even if errors occur\\n- **CoreUtils.swallow()**: Catches exceptions during shutdown to continue with remaining components\\n- **Utils.closeQuietly()**: Safe resource cleanup\\n- **CountDownLatches**: Coordinate multi-component startup/shutdown\\n- **AtomicBoolean flags**: Track shutdown state in thread-safe manner\\n\\n#### 4. Graceful Shutdown\\n- **Timeouts**: Workers use TASK_SHUTDOWN_GRACEFUL_TIMEOUT_MS (default 5000ms)\\n- **Hooks**: Register shutdown hooks that trigger stop() on JVM exit\\n- **Controlled shutdown**: Brokers support controlled shutdown mode before forceful termination\\n- **State transitions**: BrokerLifecycleManager uses state machine (RUNNING → PENDING_CONTROLLED_SHUTDOWN → SHUTTING_DOWN)\\n\\n#### 5. Thread Safety\\n- **Volatile variables**: For cross-thread visibility\\n- **Event queues**: Single-threaded processing with queued events\\n- **Executor services**: Shutdown gracefully with timeouts\\n- **Synchronized blocks**: Protect concurrent access\\n\\n### Key File References\\n\\n**Connect Lifecycle Chain**:\\n1. This is a critical design pattern for distributed systems where components have explicit dependencies.\\n\\n## Java Service Initialization Lifecycle in Kafka\\n\\n### Core Pattern\\nKafka uses a convention-based lifecycle pattern without explicit Startable/Stoppable interfaces. Instead, services implement start() and stop() methods following a consistent pattern.\\n\\n### Key Lifecycle Components\\n\\n#### 1. Kafka Connect Runtime (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/)\\n**Connect.java** (lines 65-97): The main orchestrator that manages the complete lifecycle of a Kafka Connect process.\\n- **start()**: Initializes components in order\\n  - Registers shutdown hook\\n  - Calls herder.start()\\n  - Calls rest.initializeResources()\\n- **stop()**: Stops components in reverse order (rest → herder)\\n- **ShutdownHook** (inner class): Thread that ensures graceful shutdown\\n\\n**Herder.java** (lines 64-66): Interface defining the lifecycle contract\\n- void start()\\n- void stop()\\n\\n**AbstractHerder.java** (lines 180-192): Abstract implementation providing templated lifecycle\\n- startServices(): Coordinates startup of worker, statusBackingStore, configBackingStore\\n- stopServices(): Coordinates shutdown in reverse order with proper error handling\\n\\n**Worker.java** (lines 235-285): Manages individual worker lifecycle\\n- start(): Initializes globalOffsetBackingStore, metrics, and offset committer\\n- stop(): Gracefully stops all connectors and tasks, then cleans up resources with timeout handling\\n\\n**RestServer.java** (lines 200-394): Abstract REST server implementation\\n- initializeServer(): Starts Jetty server, configures handlers and contexts\\n- stop(): Gracefully stops all handlers, REST extensions, and Jetty server with resource cleanup\\n\\n**DistributedHerder.java** (lines 156-300): Implements distributed coordination\\n- Uses AtomicBoolean stopping flag for thread-safe shutdown\\n- Manages WorkerGroupMember coordination\\n- Handles executor service shutdown with timeouts\\n\\n**ConnectRestServer.java**: Concrete implementation of RestServer\\n\\n#### 2. Kafka Broker Runtime (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/)\\n**BrokerServer.scala** (lines 729-843): Implements comprehensive broker lifecycle with explicit shutdown ordering\\n- **shutdown()** method demonstrates reverse-order shutdown pattern:\\n  1. Check controlled shutdown settings\\n  2. Stop socket server request processing\\n  3. Shutdown scheduler (critical: prevents concurrent access to other resources)\\n  4. Stop transaction coordinator\\n  5. Stop group/share coordinators\\n  6. Stop replica manager\\n  7. Shutdown alter partition manager\\n  8. Close log manager and remote storage\\n  9. Stop quota managers\\n  10. Final socket server shutdown\\n  11. Close lifecycle manager\\n\\n**BrokerLifecycleManager.scala** (lines 223-307): Manages broker state machine lifecycle\\n- **start()**: Sends StartupEvent through event queue\\n  - Initializes channel manager\\n  - Transitions to STARTING state\\n  - Sends broker registration\\n- **beginControlledShutdown()**: Graceful shutdown request\\n- **beginShutdown()**: Non-blocking shutdown initiation\\n- **close()**: Blocks until complete shutdown\\n- Event-driven architecture using KafkaEventQueue for thread-safe operations\\n\\n**KafkaRaftServer.scala**: Combined controller/broker with startup() and shutdown() methods\\n- Implements reverse-order shutdown: broker first, then controller\\n\\n#### 3. Test Framework (test-common/test-common-runtime/)\\n**KafkaClusterTestKit.java**: Demonstrates coordinated startup and shutdown of multiple broker/controller instances\\n- Uses ExecutorService for parallel startup\\n- Implements synchronized shutdown pattern\\n\\n#### 4. Mirror Maker (connect/mirror/)\\n**MirrorMaker.java** (lines 178-226): Multi-herder lifecycle coordinator\\n- **start()**: Creates CountDownLatches, starts all herders in try-finally blocks\\n- **stop()**: Stops all herders in try-finally blocks, ensuring each herder is stopped even if others fail\\n- **awaitStop()**: Waits for all herders to complete shutdown\\n\\n### Lifecycle Patterns Observed\\n\\n#### 1. Startup Ordering\\nServices are started in dependency order:\\n- Herder (manages everything)\\n  - Worker (manages connectors/tasks)\\n    - GlobalOffsetBackingStore\\n    - StatusBackingStore\\n    - ConfigBackingStore\\n  - REST server (depends on herder being ready)\\n\\n#### 2. Shutdown Ordering (Reverse Dependency Order)\\nServices are stopped in reverse order to their startup:\\n- REST server (stops accepting requests first)\\n- Herder (stops managing work)\\n  - Worker (stops connectors/tasks)\\n  - Backing stores\\n  - Status/Config stores\\n\\n#### 3. Error Handling Patterns\\n- **Try-finally blocks**: Ensure shutdown code runs even if errors occur\\n- **CoreUtils.swallow()**: Catches exceptions during shutdown to continue with remaining components\\n- **Utils.closeQuietly()**: Safe resource cleanup\\n- **CountDownLatches**: Coordinate multi-component startup/shutdown\\n- **AtomicBoolean flags**: Track shutdown state in thread-safe manner\\n\\n#### 4. Graceful Shutdown\\n- **Timeouts**: Workers use TASK_SHUTDOWN_GRACEFUL_TIMEOUT_MS (default 5000ms)\\n- **Hooks**: Register shutdown hooks that trigger stop() on JVM exit\\n- **Controlled shutdown**: Brokers support controlled shutdown mode before forceful termination\\n- **State transitions**: BrokerLifecycleManager uses state machine (RUNNING → PENDING_CONTROLLED_SHUTDOWN → SHUTTING_DOWN)\\n\\n#### 5. Thread Safety\\n- **Volatile variables**: For cross-thread visibility\\n- **Event queues**: Single-threaded processing with queued events\\n- **Executor services**: Shutdown gracefully with timeouts\\n- **Synchronized blocks**: Protect concurrent access\\n\\n### Key File References\\n\\n**Connect Lifecycle Chain**:\\n1. Connect.start() → herder.start() → (worker.start() → rest.initializeServer())\\n2. Connect.stop() → rest.stop() → herder.stop() → worker.stop()\\n\\n**Broker Lifecycle Chain**:\\n1. BrokerServer.startup() → BrokerLifecycleManager.start() → multiple component startups\\n2. BrokerServer.shutdown() → 11-step reverse-order shutdown sequence\\n\\n**Mirror Maker Pattern**:\\n- Manages multiple Herder instances\\n- Ensures all herders start even if one fails\\n- Ensures all herders stop even if one fails\\n- Uses CountDownLatches for synchronization\\n\\nThis lifecycle pattern ensures that no service attempts to use resources that have already been shut down, and that all graceful shutdown procedures are completed before the JVM terminates.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
